     <p>The <b>University of Alberta</b> (also known as <b>U of A</b> and <b>UAlberta</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> research university located in <a href="/wiki/Edmonton" title="Edmonton">Edmonton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. It was founded in 1908 by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Cameron_Rutherford" title="Alexander Cameron Rutherford">Alexander Cameron Rutherford</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Rutherford_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rutherford-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> the first premier of Alberta, and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Marshall_Tory" title="Henry Marshall Tory">Henry Marshall Tory</a> (McGill University alumni),<sup id="cite_ref-Tory_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tory-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> its first president. Its enabling legislation is the <i>Post-secondary Learning Act.</i><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university comprises four campuses in Edmonton, the Augustana Campus in Camrose, and a staff centre in downtown Calgary. The original north campus consists of 150 buildings covering 50 city blocks on the south rim of the <a href="/wiki/North_Saskatchewan_River_valley_parks_system" title="North Saskatchewan River valley parks system">North Saskatchewan River valley</a>, directly across from <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Edmonton" title="Downtown Edmonton">downtown Edmonton</a>. More than 39,000 students from across Canada and 144 other countries participate in nearly 400 programs in 18 faculties.</p> 
     <p>The University of Alberta is a major economic driver in Alberta. The university’s impact on the Alberta economy is an estimated $12.3 billion annually, or five per cent of the province’s gross domestic product.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> With more than 15,000 employees, the university is Alberta's fourth-largest employer.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Alberta has been recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a>, the <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> as one of the top five universities in Canada and one of the top 100 universities worldwide. It has graduated more than 240,000 alumni, including Governor General <a href="/wiki/Roland_Michener" title="Roland Michener">Roland Michener</a>, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Joe_Clark" title="Joe Clark">Joe Clark</a>, Chief Justice of Canada <a href="/wiki/Beverley_McLachlin" title="Beverley McLachlin">Beverley McLachlin</a>, Premier of Alberta <a href="/wiki/Peter_Lougheed" title="Peter Lougheed">Peter Lougheed</a> and Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Richard_E._Taylor" title="Richard E. Taylor">Richard E. Taylor</a>.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft">

       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Corbett_Hall_University_Of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_08A.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Corbett Hall, University of Alberta campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Alberta, a single, public provincial university, was chartered in 1906 in <a href="/wiki/Edmonton,_Alberta" title="Edmonton, Alberta" class="mw-redirect">Edmonton, Alberta</a> with the University Act<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> in the first session of the new <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Alberta" title="Legislative Assembly of Alberta">Legislative Assembly</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Premier_(Canada)" title="Premier (Canada)">Premier</a> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_C._Rutherford" title="Alexander C. Rutherford" class="mw-redirect">Alexander C. Rutherford</a> as its sponsor. The university was modelled on the American state university, with an emphasis on extension work and applied research.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The governance was modelled on Ontario's University of Toronto Act of 1906: a bicameral system consisting of a senate (faculty) responsible for academic policy, and a board of governors (citizens) controlling financial policy and having formal authority in all other matters. The president, appointed by the board, was to provide a link between the two bodies and perform institutional leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Heated wrangling took place between the cities of <a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary</a> and Edmonton over the location of the provincial capital and of the university. It was stated that the capital would be north of the North Saskatchewan River and that the university would be in a city south of it.<sup id="cite_ref-Rutherford_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rutherford-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> The city of Edmonton became the capital and the then-separate city of <a href="/wiki/Strathcona,_Alberta" title="Strathcona, Alberta">Strathcona</a> on the south bank of the river, where Premier Alexander Rutherford lived, was granted the university. When the two cities were <a href="/wiki/Amalgamation_(politics)" title="Amalgamation (politics)" class="mw-redirect">amalgamated</a> in 1912, Edmonton became both the political and academic capital.</p> 
     <p>With <a href="/wiki/Henry_Marshall_Tory" title="Henry Marshall Tory">Henry Marshall Tory</a> as its first president, the University of Alberta started operation in 1908. Forty-five students attended classes in English, mathematics and modern languages, on the top floor of the Queen Alexandra Elementary School in Strathcona, while the first campus building, Athabasca Hall, was under construction.<sup id="cite_ref-MacLeod_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacLeod-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> In a letter to <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Cameron_Rutherford" title="Alexander Cameron Rutherford">Alexander Cameron Rutherford</a> in early 1906, while he was in the process of setting up <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia" title="University of British Columbia">McGill University College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, Tory wrote, <i>&quot;If you take any steps in the direction of a working University and wish to avoid the mistakes of the past, mistakes which have fearfully handicapped other institutions, you should start on a teaching basis.&quot;</i><sup id="cite_ref-ToryQuote_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ToryQuote-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Under Tory's guidance, the university's early years were marked by recruitment of professors and construction of the first campus buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-Centenary_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Centenary-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Percy_Erskine_Nobbs" title="Percy Erskine Nobbs">Percy Erskine Nobbs</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Frank_Darling_(architect)" title="Frank Darling (architect)">Frank Darling</a> designed the master plan for the University of Alberta in 1909–10. Nobbs designed the Arts Building (1914–15), laboratories and Power House (1914). With Cecil S. Burgess, Nobbs designed the Provincial College of Medicine (1920–21).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Architect Herbert Alton Magoon designed several buildings on campus, including St. Stephen's Methodist College (1910) and the residence for professor Rupert C. Lodge (1913).<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Alberta awarded its first degrees in 1912,<sup id="cite_ref-MacLeod_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacLeod-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> the same year it established the Department of Extension. The Faculty of Medicine was established the following year,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Faculty of Agriculture began in 1915. But along with these early milestones came the First World War and the global influenza pandemic of 1918, whose toll on the university resulted in a two-month suspension of classes in the fall of 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-MacLeod_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacLeod-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite these setbacks, the university continued to grow. By 1920, it had six faculties (Arts and Sciences, Applied Science, Agriculture, Medicine, Dentistry, and Law) and two schools (Pharmacy and Accountancy). It awarded a range of degrees: Bachelor of Arts (BA), Bachelor of Science (BSc), <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science_in_Agriculture" title="Bachelor of Science in Agriculture">Bachelor of Science in Agriculture</a> (BSA), <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Laws" title="Bachelor of Laws">Bachelor of Laws</a> (LLB), <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Pharmacy" title="Bachelor of Pharmacy">Bachelor of Pharmacy</a> (PhmB), <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Divinity" title="Bachelor of Divinity">Bachelor of Divinity</a> (BD), <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Arts_(postgraduate)" title="Master of Arts (postgraduate)" class="mw-redirect">Master of Arts</a> (MA), <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Science" title="Master of Science">Master of Science</a> (MSc), and <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Laws" title="Doctor of Laws" class="mw-redirect">Doctor of Laws</a> (LLD). There were 851 male students and 251 female students, and 171 academic staff, including 14 women.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Breton Soil Plots were established at U of A's faculty of agriculture from 1929-present to provide agricultural research on fertilization, usage, crop rotations and farming practices on Gray-Luvisolic soils (Gray-Wooded), which cover many regions in western Canada. <sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The War Memorial Committee commissioned a War Memorial Pipe Organ to be erected by the <a href="/wiki/Casavant_Fr%C3%A8res" title="Casavant Fr&egrave;res">Casavant Fr&egrave;res</a> in U of A Convocation Hall in 1925 in memory of 80 University of Alberta comrades who gave up their lives during the Great War. <sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the early part of the 20th century, professional education expanded beyond the traditional fields of theology, law and medicine. Graduate training based on the German-inspired American model of specialized course work and the completion of a research thesis was introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1929, the university established a College of Education. This period of growth was to be short-lived, though, as the Great Depression and the Second World War curtailed enrolment and expansion until 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-Centenary_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Centenary-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The University also gained new public powers. In 1928, the university's senate was granted the power to oversee and appoint half of the <a href="/wiki/Alberta_Eugenics_Board" title="Alberta Eugenics Board">Alberta Eugenics Board</a>, charged with recommending individuals for sterilization.<sup id="cite_ref-Puplampu_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Puplampu-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Spurred by postwar growth in the student population and the discovery of oil in Leduc in 1947, the University of Alberta underwent expansion through the 1950s that continued through the 1960s as the baby-boom generation swelled the enrolment ranks.<sup id="cite_ref-Centenary_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Centenary-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> These two decades also saw expansion of campus buildings, including new buildings for the faculties of physical education and education, and the Cameron Library.<sup id="cite_ref-Centenary_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Centenary-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Press" title="University of Alberta Press">University of Alberta Press</a>, concentrating on western Canadian history, general science and ecology, was founded in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The policy of university education initiated in the 1960s responded to population pressure and the belief that higher education was a key to social justice and economic productivity for individuals and for society. In addition, the single-university policy in the West was changed as existing colleges of the provincial universities gained autonomy as universities. On September 19, 1960, the university opened a new 130-hectare campus in Calgary.<sup id="cite_ref-pound2005_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pound2005-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1966, the University of Calgary had been established as an autonomous institution.<sup id="cite_ref-MacLeod_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacLeod-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>From the mid-1970s to the late 1980s, the university enjoyed sustained growth, and growing inclusiveness. In 1970, the Coll&egrave;ge Saint-Jean began offering French-language instruction in arts, science and education. In 1984, the School of Native Studies was established. Buildings that had been started in the 1960s, such as Biological Sciences and the Central Academic Building, were completed in the early 1970s. Extensive renovations restored the venerable Arts Building, as well as the Athabasca and Pembina halls.<sup id="cite_ref-Centenary_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Centenary-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> New buildings completed in the early 1980s included the Business Building and the first phase of the Walter C. Mackenzie Health Sciences Centre. Another new building, the distinctive Universiade Pavilion (nicknamed the &quot;Butterdome&quot;), was completed as part of the university's preparations to host the World University Games in 1983, the first time the event was held in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-Centenary_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Centenary-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The 1990s were a time of financial constraint as the Alberta government made significant budgetary cutbacks.<sup id="cite_ref-MacLeod_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacLeod-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> But they were also a time in which the university benefited from philanthropic support. The $11-million Timms Centre for the Arts, which began construction in 1993, was made possible by a large donation from its namesake, Albert Timms.<sup id="cite_ref-Centenary_15-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Centenary-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1998, Gladys Young's $3.5-million donation to the university undergraduate scholarship fund in memory of Roland Young, who graduated from the U of A in 1928, was the largest private donation for undergraduate scholarships in the university's history.<sup id="cite_ref-pound2005_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pound2005-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The early 2000s brought substantial funding increases. High energy prices drove Alberta's energy boom resulting in multi-billion dollar government surpluses<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> and the subsequent creation of a $4.5 billion provincial post-secondary educational endowment.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2005, the university hired <a href="/wiki/Indira_Samarasekera" title="Indira Samarasekera">Indira Samarasekera</a> as its 12th president, embarking on an ambitious plan to establish itself as one of the world's top public research universities.<sup id="cite_ref-Centenary_15-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Centenary-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> These plans were hampered by the <a href="/wiki/2008_economic_downturn" title="2008 economic downturn" class="mw-redirect">2008 economic downturn</a>, and by late March 2008, the university's endowment had shrunk by more than $100 million, almost 14 per cent of its value.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The university predicted a $59-million budget shortfall in 2009<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> before provincial cuts brought that figure to $79 million.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> To close the budgetary gap, the university increased non-instructional fees by $290 per year<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> laid off teaching and support staff, and even eliminated phones in some departments (such as English and Film Studies).<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The 2013 Alberta Budget cut provincial postsecondary grants by 6.8%. The University plans to cover its resulting shortfall by reducing total spending in 2013 by 1.5%, then steeply cutting spending every year until 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UalbertaArtsBldg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Arts Building
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The U of A has about 39,000 students, including more than 7,400 graduate students<sup id="cite_ref-enrolment_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enrolment-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> and 6,400 international students representing 144 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has 3,620 academic staff along with about 15,380 support and trust staff.<sup id="cite_ref-staff_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-staff-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> University professors have won more <a href="/wiki/3M" title="3M">3M</a> Teaching Fellowships (Canada's top award for undergraduate teaching excellence) than any other Canadian university, 38 awards since 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The university offers <a href="/wiki/Post-secondary" title="Post-secondary" class="mw-redirect">post-secondary</a> education in about 200 undergraduate and 170 <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" title="Graduate school">graduate</a> programs. Tuition and fees for both fall and winter semesters are slightly more than $5,000 for a typical undergraduate student, although they vary widely by program.<sup id="cite_ref-enrolment_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enrolment-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Alberta switched from a 9-point grading scale to the more common 4-point <a href="/wiki/GPA_in_Canada" title="GPA in Canada" class="mw-redirect">grading scale</a> in September 2003. Sixty-eight Rhodes Scholars have come from the University of Alberta.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculties_and_colleges">Faculties and colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Faculties and colleges">edit</a>]</span></h3>

     <p>The university has eighteen <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(division)" title="Faculty (division)">faculties</a>:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ales.ualberta.ca/">Faculty of Agricultural, Life and Environmental Sciences</a></b> focuses on <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural</a>, biological, and <a href="/wiki/Human_resources" title="Human resources">human resources</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_School_of_Business" title="University of Alberta School of Business">Alberta School of Business</a></b> offers <a href="/wiki/MBA" title="MBA" class="mw-redirect">MBA</a>, <a href="/wiki/BCom" title="BCom" class="mw-redirect">BCom</a>, PhD, <a href="/wiki/Executive_Education" title="Executive Education" class="mw-redirect">ExecEd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Executive_MBA" title="Executive MBA" class="mw-redirect">Exec MBA</a>, and Master of Financial Management degrees.</li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Faculty_of_Arts" title="University of Alberta Faculty of Arts">Faculty of Arts</a></b> is home to a spectrum of arts programs and departments, from <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">Anthropology</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.csl.ualberta.ca/">Community Service Learning</a> to History and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Studies" title="Women's Studies" class="mw-redirect">Women's Studies</a>.</li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Augustana_Faculty" title="University of Alberta Augustana Faculty">Augustana Campus</a></b> is located in a satellite campus in <a href="/wiki/Camrose,_Alberta" title="Camrose, Alberta">Camrose, Alberta</a>. It comprises the departments of Fine Arts, Humanities, Physical Education, Science, and Social Sciences.</li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Facult%C3%A9_Saint-Jean" title="University of Alberta Facult&eacute; Saint-Jean">Campus Saint-Jean</a></b> is a francophone faculty with programs in Sciences, Fine Arts and Languages, Social Sciences, and Education.</li> 
      <li><b><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.uofaweb.ualberta.ca/education/">Faculty of Education</a></b> offers undergraduate and graduate degrees in elementary and secondary education, or a combined program.</li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Faculty_of_Engineering" title="University of Alberta Faculty of Engineering">Faculty of Engineering</a></b> offers undergraduate degrees in five engineering departments. Students can choose to specialize in the following disciplines: <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Engineering" title="Chemical Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Chemical Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Civil_Engineering" title="Civil Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Civil Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_Engineering" title="Computer Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Computer Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_Engineering" title="Electrical Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Electrical Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering_Physics" title="Engineering Physics" class="mw-redirect">Engineering Physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Materials_Engineering" title="Materials Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Materials Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_Engineering" title="Mechanical Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Mechanical Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mining_Engineering" title="Mining Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Mining Engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_Engineering" title="Petroleum Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Petroleum Engineering</a>.</li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Faculty_of_Extension" title="University of Alberta Faculty of Extension">Faculty of Extension</a></b> offers more than 300 courses in over 30 programs focusing on lifelong <a href="/wiki/Continuing_Education" title="Continuing Education" class="mw-redirect">Continuing Education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Professional_Development" title="Professional Development" class="mw-redirect">Professional Development</a>. Among the faculty's contributions to Alberta's educational and cultural life are the creation of the <a href="/wiki/CKUA" title="CKUA" class="mw-redirect">CKUA</a> public radio station in 1927 and the Banff School of Fine Arts in 1933.</li> 
      <li><b>Faculty of Graduate Studies and Research</b> maintains more than 170 programs in <a href="/wiki/Graduate_studies" title="Graduate studies" class="mw-redirect">graduate studies</a>.</li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Faculty_of_Law" title="University of Alberta Faculty of Law">Faculty of Law</a></b> is the oldest law school in Western Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> It is home to interdisciplinary institutes of constitutional studies, health law, science policy and law reform in Alberta.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Faculty_of_Medicine_and_Dentistry" title="University of Alberta Faculty of Medicine and Dentistry">Faculty of Medicine &amp; Dentistry</a></b> has 20 departments, seven divisions, eight research groups, and 31 centres and institutes. The faculty is internationally known for research in diabetes, obesity, virology, cardiology, cancer and spinal injury rehabilitation.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>Faculty of Native Studies</b> is Canada's only stand-alone faculty of native studies. The faculty began offering a master's program in the 2012-13 academic year.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>Faculty of Nursing</b> is one of Canada's largest nursing faculties, and was the first in Canada to offer a fully funded PhD program.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Faculty_of_Pharmacy_and_Pharmaceutical_Sciences" title="University of Alberta Faculty of Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Sciences">Faculty of Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Sciences</a></b> is one of Canada's largest and finest pharmacy faculties. Its students excel nationally, achieving the highest combined score on the Pharmacy Examining Board of Canada exam in 2009 and 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>Faculty of Physical Education and Recreation</b> focuses on the studies of human movement through sport science, <a href="/wiki/Kinesiology" title="Kinesiology">kinesiology</a>, physical education, physical activity and health, and tourism studies.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The Faculty of Physical Education offers four undergraduate programs: Bachelor of Arts in Recreation, Sport and Tourism; Bachelor of Physical Education; Bachelor of Physical Education/Bachelor of Education (five-year combined degree offered in conjunction with the Faculty of Education); and Bachelor of Science in Kinesiology.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>Faculty of Rehabilitation Medicine</b> is North America's only stand-alone faculty dedicated to rehabilitation science, physical therapy, occupational therapy and speech-language pathology. The faculty is a research leader in musculoskeletal health, spinal cord injuries, seniors' health, and use of communication technologies to support community care.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>School of Public Health</b> was established in March 2006 as Canada's first stand-alone faculty with a sole focus on public health.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2012, it became the only school in Canada and only the second outside the United States to be accredited by the U.S. Council on Education for Public Health.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>Faculty of Science</b> is made up of seven departments (Biological Sciences, Chemistry, Computing Science, Earth and Atmospheric Sciences, Mathematical and Statistical Sciences, Physics and Psychology.) The faculty includes 6 Steacie Award winners, 16 winners of Rutherford Awards for Excellence in Undergraduate Teaching, 26 Canada Research Chairs, 5 iCORE Chairs, 3 NSERC Chairs, 2 Alberta Ingenuity Centres of Excellence, and 10 members of the Royal Society of Canada. It has more than 70 bachelor of science (BSc) programs in 39 subject areas.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The university also has two affiliated colleges:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/St._Joseph%27s_College,_Edmonton" title="St. Joseph's College, Edmonton">St. Joseph's College</a></b> offers undergraduate courses in applied ethics, philosophy, religious education and theology, for credit in degree programs with arts options. The college also offers specific courses for education students intending to teach within Alberta's Catholic school system.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>St. Stephen's College</b> offers graduate degree, diploma and certificate programs in theological studies, with courses designed to allow distance learning.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Rutherford_Humanities_and_Social_Sciences_Library_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Rutherford_Humanities_and_Social_Sciences_Library_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada.jpg/220px-Rutherford_Humanities_and_Social_Sciences_Library_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Rutherford_Humanities_and_Social_Sciences_Library_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada.jpg/330px-Rutherford_Humanities_and_Social_Sciences_Library_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Rutherford_Humanities_and_Social_Sciences_Library_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada.jpg/440px-Rutherford_Humanities_and_Social_Sciences_Library_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption">

       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Business_Building_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Business_Building_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_02.jpg/170px-Business_Building_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_02.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Business_Building_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_02.jpg/255px-Business_Building_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Business_Building_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_02.jpg/340px-Business_Building_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_02.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Business_Building_University_of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Winspear Business Reference Library

      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Alberta library system received a tremendous boost with the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Rutherford_Library" title="Rutherford Library">Rutherford Library</a> in May 1951, and now has one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Research_library" title="Research library" class="mw-redirect">research libraries</a> systems in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2012, according to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Research_Libraries" title="Association of Research Libraries">Association of Research Libraries</a>, the library system is rated 11th in North America and is the second-largest, by number of volumes held, among all Canadian universities, after the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a> Library.<sup id="cite_ref-Fisher_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fisher-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> With over 10.6 million items combined with online access to more than one million electronic books and more than 1,400 electronic databases, the library system ranks first in Canada in terms of the number of volumes per student.<sup id="cite_ref-facilities_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facilities-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The library system comprises the following specialty libraries:<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b>Augustana Faculty Library</b></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Biblioth%C3%A8que_Saint-Jean" title="Biblioth&egrave;que Saint-Jean">Biblioth&egrave;que Saint-Jean</a></b></li> 
      <li><b>Book and Record Depository (BARD)</b></li> 
      <li><b>Cameron Library</b> (Science &amp; Technology) 
       <ul> 
        <li>Data Library</li> 
       </ul> </li> 
      <li><b>Herbert T. Coutts Library</b> (Education &amp; Physical Education)</li> 
      <li><b>John A. Weir Memorial Law Library</b></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/John_W._Scott_Health_Sciences_Library" title="John W. Scott Health Sciences Library" class="mw-redirect">John W. Scott Health Sciences Library</a></b></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Rutherford_Library" title="Rutherford Library">Rutherford Library</a></b> (Humanities &amp; Social Sciences) 
       <ul> 
        <li>Bruce Peel Special Collections Library</li> 
       </ul> </li> 
      <li><b>St. Joseph's College Library</b></li> 
      <li><b>Winspear Business Reference Library</b></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The university is home to an <a href="/wiki/American_Library_Association" title="American Library Association">American Library Association</a>-accredited <b>School of Library and Information Studies,</b> which offers a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Library_and_Information_Studies" title="Master of Library and Information Studies" class="mw-redirect">Master of Library and Information Studies</a> (MLIS) program.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> The school is housed in <a href="/wiki/Rutherford_Library" title="Rutherford Library">Rutherford South</a>, the original four-storey brick, marble and oak main campus library, which opened in 1951.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Botanic_Garden">Botanic Garden</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Botanic Garden">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The University of Alberta houses the Devonian Botanic Garden in <a href="/wiki/Devon,_Alberta" title="Devon, Alberta">Devon, Alberta</a>. The garden runs a series of winter hardiness trials on trees, shrubs, herbs, annuals and bulbs. The garden collection consists of: Primula, Meconopsis, Allium Rosa (shrub), Alpines; herbs and plants traditionally used by Aboriginal peoples. There is a microfungus collection and a herbarium which ccontains over 4,800 different livery genotypic filamentous fungi. <sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NINT.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/NINT.JPG/220px-NINT.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/NINT.JPG/330px-NINT.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/NINT.JPG/440px-NINT.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NINT.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The National Institute for Nanotechnology
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Housing over 400 distinct research laboratories, the University of Alberta is one of the leading research universities in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is a member of the <a href="/wiki/U15_(universities)" title="U15 (universities)" class="mw-redirect">U15</a> universities and the <a href="/wiki/Worldwide_Universities_Network" title="Worldwide Universities Network">Worldwide Universities Network</a>, an organization of 18 universities on six continents. The university receives nearly $500 million each year for research from external sources.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Alberta is also the national scientific and administrative headquarters for:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sfmn.ales.ualberta.ca/">Sustainable Forest Management Network</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Canadian_Obesity_Network" title="Canadian Obesity Network">Canadian Obesity Network</a></li> 
      <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.fwalive.ualberta.ca/home/">Canadian Centre for Ethnomusicology</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.fwalive.ualberta.ca/home/">folkwaysAlive!</a> in partnership with <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.folkways.si.edu">Smithsonian Folkways Recordings</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Researchers at the University of Alberta have made significant discoveries in a number of fields.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_and_medical_research">Scientific and medical research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Scientific and medical research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 1917, physics professor Robert Boyle developed sonar.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Biochemistry professor James Collip played a key role in discovering insulin by refining the pancreatic extract obtained by Frederick Banting, Charles Best and John Macleod so it could be used in humans.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Chemistry professor Raymond Lemieux was the first to synthesize sucrose. The breakthrough laid the groundwork for new antibiotics and blood reagents, anti-rejection drugs for organ transplants, and better treatments for leukemia and hemophilia.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1956, surgeon John Callaghan performed the first successful open-heart surgery.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Canada's first organ transplant research group was established at the University of Alberta on April 2, 1970, by the Medical Research Council.<sup id="cite_ref-pound2005_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pound2005-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1995, engineer Robert Burrell used nanotechnology to develop a form of silver that could be made into a bandage for burns and other wounds. The dressings are now used worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Medical researchers <a href="/wiki/James_Shapiro_(physician)" title="James Shapiro (physician)">James Shapiro</a>, Jonathan Lakey and Edmond Ryan developed the <a href="/wiki/Edmonton_Protocol" title="Edmonton Protocol" class="mw-redirect">Edmonton Protocol</a>, a revolutionary treatment for <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus_type_1" title="Diabetes mellitus type 1">Type 1</a> <a href="/wiki/Diabetes" title="Diabetes" class="mw-redirect">diabetes</a> that enables people with the disease to break their <a href="/wiki/Insulin" title="Insulin">insulin</a> dependence.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The first patient was treated in 1999. As of 2006, the project is developed through the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.islet.ca/">Clinical Islet Transplant Program</a>.</p> 
     <p>In 2008, medical researcher David Bundle and his colleagues Glen Armstrong and Pavel Kitov made a breakthrough in treating E. coli infection by creating a drug that prevents the E. coli bacterium from making contact with kidney cells.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Michael Houghton, Canada Excellence Research Chair and Li Ka Shing Chair in Virology, showed that a vaccine created from one strain of the hepatitis C virus can be effective against all known strains of the virus. Houghton was also the researcher who originally identified the hepatitis C virus. The discovery paves the way for developing a vaccine to prevent future hepatitis C infections.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nanotechnology_research">Nanotechnology research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Nanotechnology research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In June 2006, a $120-million building for the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Nanotechnology" title="National Institute for Nanotechnology">National Institute for Nanotechnology</a> (NINT) was opened on campus. The NINT complex is one of the world’s most technologically advanced research facilities, housing the quietest and cleanest laboratory space in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> NINT occupies five floors of the new building, with the top two floors being reserved by the university for <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a>-related research. Some staff members have been jointly recruited by the <a href="/wiki/National_Research_Council_of_Canada" title="National Research Council of Canada" class="mw-redirect">NRC</a> and the University of Alberta.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arctic_research">Arctic research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Arctic research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Alberta is home to the Canadian Circumpolar Institute, which supports research into social and environmental issues including climate change, cultural identity and natural resource development.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2011, researchers at the University of Alberta linked the reproductive ecology of polar bears in Canada's Hudson Bay with decreasing litter sizes and loss of sea ice.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Cattle researcher Roy Berg revolutionized the world's beef industry with his innovations in crossbreeding, which led to a 30 to 40 per cent increase in production and contributed to Alberta's world leadership in beef production.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy.2C_oilsands_and_environment">Energy, oilsands and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Energy, oilsands and environment">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In the 1920s, engineering professor Karl Clark developed a hot-water extraction process to separate bitumen from oilsands. Geology professor Charlie Stelck's idea to search for oil and gas deposits near ancient coral reefs led to the discovery of oil in Leduc, Alberta, in 1947 and in the Pembina Oil Field in 1953. Today, more than 1,000 researchers at the University of Alberta are working together on oilsands issues and their environmental effects, including carbon capture and storage, tailings-pond reclamation and water preservation.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_60-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>University of Alberta’s SLOWPOKE-2 non-power reactor operating licence was renewed and will be valid from July 1, 2013 until June 30, 2023. The <a href="/wiki/SLOWPOKE_reactor" title="SLOWPOKE reactor">SLOWPOKE reactor</a> is used for research and education <sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The university participated in the initial development of the <a href="/wiki/Mizar_system" title="Mizar system">Mizar system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">asteroid</a> <a href="/wiki/99906_Uofalberta" title="99906 Uofalberta">99906 Uofalberta</a> is <a href="/wiki/Meanings_of_asteroid_names" title="Meanings of asteroid names" class="mw-redirect">named in the university's honour</a>, in part because the initials of its motto <i>Quaecumque Vera</i> (&quot;Whatsoever things are true&quot;) appeared in the object's <a href="/wiki/Provisional_designation_in_astronomy" title="Provisional designation in astronomy">provisional designation</a> <span class="nowrap">2002 QV<sub>53</sub></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reputation">Reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Reputation">edit</a>]</span></h2>

           <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Canadian_university_rankings" title="Template:Canadian university rankings"><span title="View this template" style="">v</span></a></li>

          </ul> 
         </div> </td>
