     </table> 
     <p>The University of Alberta consistently ranks among the top five universities in Canada and among the top public research universities worldwide. In 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> ranked the university 108th overall in the world. The <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics Ranking of World Universities</a> rated the university 69th in the world in July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2012-2013 <a href="/wiki/University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance" title="University Ranking by Academic Performance" class="mw-redirect">University Ranking by Academic Performance</a> rated the university 61st in the world and fourth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2012, the University of Alberta was named one of &quot;Canada's Greenest Employers&quot; by Mediacorp Canada Inc. for the fourth straight year.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was also named one of <a href="/wiki/Alberta%27s_Top_Employers" title="Alberta's Top Employers" class="mw-redirect">Alberta's Top Employers</a> for the fourth consecutive year in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Globe_and_Mail" title="Globe and Mail" class="mw-redirect">The Globe and Mail</a>'</i>s University Report reflects the opinions of more than 35,000 undergraduates who responded to some 100 questions about their respective universities.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Alberta received scores of B+ and above in the following categories:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>overall quality of education</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>ease of course registration</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>libraries</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>technology</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The University has also been the subject of several recent scandals. In 2011, the school's dean of medicine resigned after plagiarizing much of his graduation address.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, the University's Psychiatry department chair was placed on leave before officially beginning his duties after allegations emerged of an inappropriate sexual relationship with a patient.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The university has five distributed campus facilities including, in addition to the North Campus, two auxiliary satellites: Campus Saint-Jean in southeast Edmonton, and Augustana Campus in <a href="/wiki/Camrose,_Alberta" title="Camrose, Alberta">Camrose</a>, 90 kilometres southeast of Edmonton. An extensively renovated and refurbished historic <a href="/wiki/The_Bay" title="The Bay" class="mw-redirect">Hudson's Bay</a> department store in downtown Edmonton, renamed Enterprise Square, serves as a campus for adult students belonging to the Faculty of Extension. The university also owns a set of large parcels of mostly undeveloped land (currently used as an experimental farm and the site of several agricultural and sports facilities) slightly south of the main campus, called South Campus (previously the University Farm), in which an entire new university complex of similar magnitude to the North Campus will gradually be constructed.</p> 
     <p>Detailed Google Maps views and 360-degree interactive panoramas of the campus can be seen on the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.campusmap.ualberta.ca/">University of Alberta website.</a></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Campus">North Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: North Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:U_of_A.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/U_of_A.jpg/220px-U_of_A.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/U_of_A.jpg/330px-U_of_A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/U_of_A.jpg/440px-U_of_A.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:U_of_A.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The University of Alberta overlooks the North Saskatchewan River valley and downtown Edmonton.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The North Campus is the original location of the University of Alberta. Located on the southern banks of the <a href="/wiki/North_Saskatchewan_River" title="North Saskatchewan River">North Saskatchewan River</a>, it has 150 buildings on 92 hectares (230&nbsp;acres) of land.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Architect <a href="/wiki/Barton_Myers" title="Barton Myers">Barton Myers</a> completed the long-range campus plan in 1969 and continued as a planner for the University until 1978.</p> 
     <p>The distinctive cupola of the Dentistry/Pharmacy Centre on North Campus was featured in a commemorative stamp issued by Canada Post in 2008, the year of the university's centenary.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Campus">South Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: South Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Located two kilometres south of the North Campus, the South Campus is much larger in terms of land area. The two campuses are linked by the convenient high-speed <a href="/wiki/Edmonton_Transit_System#LRT" title="Edmonton Transit System">Light Rail Transit</a>. <a href="/wiki/South_Campus/Fort_Edmonton_Park" title="South Campus/Fort Edmonton Park" class="mw-redirect">The transit station</a> is near <b>Foote Field</b> and the <b>Saville Community Sports Centre</b>, forming a natural gateway to the new campus architectural model. Since South Campus LRT opened in April 2009, the U of A became the only university in Canada with four LRT/subway stations on its campuses (Along with <a href="/wiki/University_(ETS)" title="University (ETS)" class="mw-redirect">University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health_Sciences/Jubilee" title="Health Sciences/Jubilee" class="mw-redirect">Health Sciences/Jubilee</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bay/Enterprise_Square" title="Bay/Enterprise Square" class="mw-redirect">Bay/Enterprise Square</a> stations).</p> 
     <p>Much of the university's agricultural research in food safety and crop use for food and industrial products happens at the Edmonton Research Station Experimental Farms on South Campus. This campus is also home to the Saville Community Sports Centre, a 32,500-square-metre, multi-use recreation facility that hosts 14 varsity teams and several community sports clubs.</p> 
     <p>Preliminary long-range development thinking for South Campus implies it may become an expanding academic and research extension of the North Campus, with rapid development over the next few decades.<sup id="cite_ref-LRDP_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRDP-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> New architectural guidelines, differing from those of the North Campus might encourage a somewhat more consistent, high quality, aesthetic architectural style. With a large expanse of land available, significant green space will be incorporated to provide a park-like context overall.<sup id="cite_ref-LRDP_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LRDP-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_Saint-Jean">Campus Saint-Jean</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Campus Saint-Jean">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Facult%C3%A9_Saint-Jean" title="University of Alberta Facult&eacute; Saint-Jean">Campus Saint-Jean</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Francophone" title="Francophone">francophone</a> campus located five kilometres east of the main campus, in <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Doon,_Edmonton" title="Bonnie Doon, Edmonton">Bonnie Doon</a>. It is the only French-language university campus west of <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a>. Due to increasing enrolment, the Campus Saint-Jean is currently undergoing expansion, acquiring new laboratory and classroom spaces. Students at Campus Saint-Jean currently may pursue Bachelor's degrees in the sciences or arts, or complete their first year of Engineering, after which they often transfer to the University of Alberta's main campus. Bilingual Nursing and Business programs are also available.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Augustana_Campus">Augustana Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Augustana Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Augustana_Faculty" title="University of Alberta Augustana Faculty">Augustana Campus</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Camrose,_Alberta" title="Camrose, Alberta">Camrose</a>, a small city in rural Alberta about 100&nbsp;km southeast of Edmonton. In 2004, the former <a href="/wiki/Augustana_University_College" title="Augustana University College">Augustana University College</a> in Camrose merged with the University of Alberta, thus creating the new satellite Augustana Campus. Students enrolled at the Augustana Campus currently may pursue four-year Bachelor's degrees in arts, sciences, or music.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enterprise_Square">Enterprise Square</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Enterprise Square">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Enterprise Square opened for business January 15, 2008 on the north side of the <a href="/wiki/North_Saskatchewan" title="North Saskatchewan" class="mw-redirect">North Saskatchewan</a> river in downtown <a href="/wiki/Edmonton" title="Edmonton">Edmonton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> It is located in the historical building previously occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company" title="Hudson's Bay Company">Hudson's Bay Company</a>. The building underwent major renovations. Currently, Enterprise Square houses the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Faculty_of_Extension" title="University of Alberta Faculty of Extension">University of Alberta Faculty of Extension</a>, the professional development activities of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_School_of_Business" title="University of Alberta School of Business">Alberta School of Business</a>, the Alberta Business Family Institute, and the Design Gallery. It is also the home of the University of Alberta Alumni Association.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_developments_and_investment_in_health_and_science">Recent developments and investment in health and science</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Recent developments and investment in health and science">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>$1.6&nbsp;billion in construction has recently been undertaken at the university related to fields in health and science. These projects greatly expand the University of Alberta's research capacity in the field of health in particular. The University of Alberta attracts approximately $500&nbsp;million in external research funding a year, the second highest in Canada;<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> this funding is expected to increase due to added state-of-the-art research and teaching capacity.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Centennial_Centre_for_Interdisciplinary_Science">Centennial Centre for Interdisciplinary Science</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Centennial Centre for Interdisciplinary Science">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>One of the recent major projects, completed in the spring of 2011 with its grand opening on September 23, 2011, was the $400-million, state-of-the-art Centennial Centre for Interdisciplinary Science (CCIS),<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> a facility for interdisciplinary research groups, as well as the Department of Physics, the Faculty of Science offices and the Interdepartmental Science Students' Society's office. Three buildings – V-Wing (a large one-floor building composed of 10 lecture halls, of which two will remain), the Avadh Bhatia Physics Building (a six-storey building formerly housing the Department of Physics offices and laboratories), and the old Centre for Subatomic Research<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> – were demolished to make way for CCIS.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Edmonton_Clinic_Health_Academy">Edmonton Clinic Health Academy</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Edmonton Clinic Health Academy">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Edmonton Clinic (formerly the Health Science Ambulatory Learning Centre) is a joint project with Alberta Health Services, and consists of two separate buildings. Construction started in 2008 on the multidisciplinary health science facilities totalling $909 million and 170,000 square metres surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Health_Sciences/Jubilee_LRT_Station" title="Health Sciences/Jubilee LRT Station">Health Sciences LRT Station</a>. Edmonton Clinic South (now known as <a href="/wiki/Edmonton_Clinic" title="Edmonton Clinic">Kaye Edmonton Clinic</a>), a nine-storey building, will focus on patient care and house most of the medical and dental clinics, while the <a href="/wiki/Edmonton_Clinic_Health_Academy" title="Edmonton Clinic Health Academy">Edmonton Clinic Health Academy</a> is a six-storey building that is the home of interdisciplinary health research and education currently held at the university. The <a href="/wiki/Edmonton_Clinic_Health_Academy" title="Edmonton Clinic Health Academy">Edmonton Clinic Health Academy</a>, owned and operated by the University of Alberta, officially opened in January 2012. The <a href="/wiki/Edmonton_Clinic" title="Edmonton Clinic">Kaye Edmonton Clinic</a>, owned and operated by Alberta Health Services, opened in December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_Research_Innovation_Facilities">Health Research Innovation Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Health Research Innovation Facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Centre_for_Pharmacy_and_Health_Research_University_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Centre_for_Pharmacy_and_Health_Research_University_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg/220px-Centre_for_Pharmacy_and_Health_Research_University_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Centre_for_Pharmacy_and_Health_Research_University_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg/330px-Centre_for_Pharmacy_and_Health_Research_University_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Centre_for_Pharmacy_and_Health_Research_University_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg/440px-Centre_for_Pharmacy_and_Health_Research_University_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Centre_for_Pharmacy_and_Health_Research_University_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Katz Group Centre for Pharmacy and Health Research
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Two new $300-million buildings adjacent to the Heritage Medical Research Centre building on the main campus, along with existing health-care and health research facilities and the Edmonton Clinic Health Academy, form a health precinct of two city blocks dedicated to health research, education and patient care. The newest facilities form a translational research centre designed to create an environment for innovative &quot;bench-to-bedside&quot; health research by increasing interaction between researchers and clinicians focused on common medical issues. A total of 65,000 square metres (699,700 square feet) gross area constructed on two sites contribute to research by allowing the university to hire over 100 additional biomedical and health researchers. This is projected to result in a doubling of research funding by 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Katz Group Centre for Pharmacy and Health Research</b></p> 
     <p>The hub of the complex is the Katz Group Centre for Pharmacy and Health Research (formerly HRIF West), an eight-storey building that provides the main entrance to the complex and becomes the critical link between Medical Sciences Building and Heritage Medical Research Centre. The Katz Group Centre is a teaching and research facility. It is home to the Li Ka Shing Institute of Virology, led by scientific director Lorne Tyrrell, MD, PhD, and includes some of the world's top virologists, including Michael Houghton, PhD, Canada Excellence Research Chair and Li Ka Shing Chair in Virology, who co-led the team that discovered the <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_C" title="Hepatitis C">hepatitis C</a> virus during his previous career in private industry. The facility is located on the corner of 89 Avenue and 114 Street in Edmonton, Alberta.</p> 
     <p><b>Li Ka Shing Centre for Health Research Innovation</b></p> 
     <p>The Li Ka Shing Centre for Health Research Innovation (formerly HRIF East) anchors the southeast corner of the health precinct and is also home to the Alberta Diabetes Institute (ADI). Both the east and west buildings of HRIF are linked at every floor to the Heritage Medical Research Centre with the exception of Level 1 of HRIF West. The facility is dedicated to health research and boasts state-of-the-art laboratories for top researchers, including several Canada Research Chairs.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The facility is named in honour of a gift in 2010 of $28 million from the Li Ka Shing (Canada) Foundation that helped establish the Li Ka Shing Institute of Virology ($25M) and a joint PhD program ($3M) between the university's Faculty of Medicine &amp; Dentistry and Shantou University Medical College in China.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> As of fall 2012, this remains the largest single cash gift to the University of Alberta. The facility is located on the corner of 89 Avenue and 112 Street in Edmonton, Alberta.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Students_Union_Building_University_Of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Students_Union_Building_University_Of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg/220px-Students_Union_Building_University_Of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Students_Union_Building_University_Of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg/330px-Students_Union_Building_University_Of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Students_Union_Building_University_Of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg/440px-Students_Union_Building_University_Of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Students_Union_Building_University_Of_Alberta_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_01A.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Students' Union Building
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Students%27_Union" title="University of Alberta Students' Union">University of Alberta Students' Union</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Undergraduate students are represented by the Students' Union (SU). Graduate students are represented by the Graduate Students' Association (GSA).</p> 
     <p>In 1946 the university student council met to consider possible blueprints for a new building, including a large auditorium, during a time when veterans were returning to complete their interrupted studies. The new building was financed by a series of mechanisms, and the completed structure opened in 1967. The Students' Union Building (SUB) has been expanded twice since its original construction. Along with the auditorium, named after former president <a href="/wiki/Myer_Horowitz" title="Myer Horowitz">Myer Horowitz</a>, it holds a number of services and businesses owned and operated by the Students' Union, as well as services owned and operated by the University of Alberta, including the University Bookstore.</p> 
     <p>There are nearly 450 student groups on campus serving students interested in academic, cultural, recreational and political involvement.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Gateway_(newspaper)" title="The Gateway (newspaper)">The Gateway</a></i> is the official student newspaper. Fully autonomous, it publishes &quot;most Wednesdays.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also has a monthly student newspaper, <i>The Dagligtale</i>, published at Augustana Campus in <a href="/wiki/Camrose,_Alberta" title="Camrose, Alberta">Camrose, Alberta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residences">Residences</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Residences">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Alberta offers a wide range of residences on its campuses. Though a majority of students live off-campus, a significant number from outside Edmonton in early years of their post-secondary education opt to live in residences operated by the university's Residence Services.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The student group representing all students living in residences is the Residence Halls Association (RHA).<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Lister_Centre" title="Lister Centre">Lister Centre</a></b> is a large residence complex of four towers, occupied mainly by first- and second-year students. It provides a full-care boarding package, with hospitality programs to help integrate new students into university life. The complex offers a large number of furnished single and double <a href="/wiki/Dormitory" title="Dormitory">dormitory</a> style rooms with common kitchens and living areas. There is a large cafeteria in the central building of the complex. Lister is the largest residence on campus with a population of 1,800.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>HUB International</b> is the second-largest residence on campus with a population of 850. It contains a combination of student apartments and small storefronts. The apartments are a mix of bachelor suites, double and quadruple bedroom apartments. The 957-foot-long (292&nbsp;m) design, by architect <a href="/wiki/Barton_Myers" title="Barton Myers">Barton Myers</a>, has an interior corridor housing businesses and restaurants that can be viewed from the apartments above, giving it the feel of a residential street. The official student group for HUB residents is the HUB Community Association (HCA)<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>International House</b> is a residence designed for international students and a few Canadian students interested in living with international students. It offers modern, well-equipped single bedrooms with common kitchens and living spaces, both furnished and unfurnished.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>Newton Place</b> is a highrise offering an apartment-style facility for older students and student couples.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>East Campus Village</b> comprises houses and walk-up townhouses, offering older and married students a modern multi-room facility.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>Michener Park</b> offers older students a well-developed, apartment-style facility near the South Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/St._Joseph%27s_College_Residence,_Edmonton" title="St. Joseph's College Residence, Edmonton" class="mw-redirect">St. Joseph's College Residence</a></b> operates an all-male residence, independent of the university's official residence service. The college also operates an all-female residence located in the HUB Mall Residence, and a summer residence from May through August.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>R&eacute;sidence Saint-Jean</b> operates a modern apartment-style, French-language oriented residence on Campus Saint-Jean, about six kilometres east of the North Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>Augustana Faculty Residences</b> comprise two distinct complexes. The 350-room First Year Complex is similar in style to (though much smaller than) Lister Centre, and is composed entirely of double rooms. Across a small ravine from the rest of the campus is another compound of seven smaller buildings (six residences and a common area) known collectively as the &quot;Ravine Complex,&quot; which houses 224 students in their second to fourth year.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Augustana is the only U of A faculty with a residence requirement whereby, with certain exceptions, all students are expected to spend their first year in residence on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>Graduate Residence</b> is the University of Alberta's newest residence, consisting of four buildings located in the East Campus community. It offers fully furnished walk-up apartments (studio or two-bedroom) and grants priority to graduate students and students in medicine and dentistry, pharmacy, and law.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Greek societies were banned at the University of Alberta until 1930 after a public campaign. Today the Greek population counts more than 500 involved and active students on campus. There are many notable Greek alumni from the U of A, including former Alberta premier <a href="/wiki/Peter_Lougheed" title="Peter Lougheed">Peter Lougheed</a>, scientist <a href="/wiki/Jay_Ingram" title="Jay Ingram">Jay Ingram</a>, former Conservative minister <a href="/wiki/Jim_Prentice" title="Jim Prentice">Jim Prentice</a>, current M.P. <a href="/wiki/Linda_Duncan" title="Linda Duncan">Linda Duncan</a> and prolific Canadian author <a href="/wiki/W.O._Mitchell" title="W.O. Mitchell" class="mw-redirect">W.O. Mitchell</a>.</p> 
     <p>The female fraternities on campus, recognized through the National Pan-Hellenic Conference, are <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Delta" title="Alpha Gamma Delta">Alpha Gamma Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Gamma" title="Delta Gamma">Delta Gamma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Theta" title="Kappa Alpha Theta">Kappa Alpha Theta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pi_Beta_Phi" title="Pi Beta Phi">Pi Beta Phi</a>, and Ceres.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> The male fraternities on campus, as recognized by the Interfraternity Council, are <a href="/wiki/Delta_Chi" title="Delta Chi">Delta Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Upsilon" title="Delta Upsilon">Delta Upsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farmhouse" title="Farmhouse">Farmhouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theta_Chi" title="Theta Chi">Theta Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Sigma" title="Kappa Sigma">Kappa Sigma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lambda_Chi_Alpha" title="Lambda Chi Alpha">Lambda Chi Alpha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pi_Kappa_Alpha" title="Pi Kappa Alpha">Pi Kappa Alpha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Gamma_Delta" title="Phi Gamma Delta">Phi Gamma Delta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Phi_Delta_Theta" title="Phi Delta Theta">Phi Delta Theta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> The IFC also recognizes the Alpha Psi local sorority as a member.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Services_for_Aboriginal_Peoples">Services for Aboriginal Peoples</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Services for Aboriginal Peoples">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Alberta provides first-year welcome-week and bridging programs specifically for Aboriginal students. The Faculty of Native Studies was designed to meet the knowledge needs of First Nations, M&eacute;tis and Inuit students, and to promote research into Aboriginal issues. The university also has outreach programs that bring young people to campus from Aboriginal communities throughout Alberta through summer science camps. The university’s Aboriginal Teacher Education Program at Blue Quills First Nations College was developed in partnership with specific Aboriginal communities to meet local needs. The Rupertsland Centre for M&eacute;tis Research (RCMR) was established in May 2011 as an Academic Centre under the Faculty of Native Studies at the University of Alberta. The RCMR is a four-way partnership between the University of Alberta, Advanced Education and Technology, the M&eacute;tis Nation of Alberta and the Rupertsland Institute.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Alberta_Universiade_Pavilion_Butterdome_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_03A.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/University_of_Alberta_Universiade_Pavilion_Butterdome_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_03A.jpg/220px-University_of_Alberta_Universiade_Pavilion_Butterdome_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_03A.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/University_of_Alberta_Universiade_Pavilion_Butterdome_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_03A.jpg/330px-University_of_Alberta_Universiade_Pavilion_Butterdome_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_03A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/University_of_Alberta_Universiade_Pavilion_Butterdome_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_03A.jpg/440px-University_of_Alberta_Universiade_Pavilion_Butterdome_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_03A.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Alberta_Universiade_Pavilion_Butterdome_Edmonton_Alberta_Canada_03A.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> South side of the Butterdome sports complex (the 
        <a href="/wiki/Universiade_Pavilion" title="Universiade Pavilion">Universiade Pavilion</a>).
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Alberta is represented in <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">Canadian Interuniversity Sport</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Alberta_Golden_Bears" title="Alberta Golden Bears">Alberta Golden Bears</a> (men's) and the <a href="/wiki/Alberta_Pandas" title="Alberta Pandas">Alberta Pandas</a> (women's). U of A teams have won 61 national championships, in a wider variety of sports than any other Canadian university.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alberta_Golden_Bears">Alberta Golden Bears</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Alberta Golden Bears">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Alberta_Golden_Bears" title="Alberta Golden Bears">Alberta Golden Bears</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Golden Bears hockey team has won 48 Canada West championships and made 18 appearances in the CIS <a href="/wiki/University_Cup" title="University Cup" class="mw-redirect">University Cup</a> finals, winning an unprecedented 13 times.<sup id="cite_ref-DeptAthleticsMen_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeptAthleticsMen-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Thirteen Golden Bears players have gone on to play in the National Hockey League.<sup id="cite_ref-DeptAthleticsMen_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeptAthleticsMen-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alberta_Pandas">Alberta Pandas</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Alberta Pandas">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>As of 2012, the Pandas <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a> team has won the Canada West Conference 11 times in the 15-year history of competition.<sup id="cite_ref-DeptAthleticsWomen_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeptAthleticsWomen-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, they have claimed the national championship seven times. When the Pandas lost the CIS championship game in March 2005, it ended a 103-game undefeated streak.<sup id="cite_ref-DeptAthleticsWomen_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeptAthleticsWomen-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Pandas volleyball team are frequent national contenders. They have won nine Canada West championships since 1994-95 and seven CIS championships over the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_and_Gold_Soccer_Academy">Green and Gold Soccer Academy</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Green and Gold Soccer Academy">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Green and Gold Soccer Academy is the U of A's soccer centre of excellence. The academy's goal is to bring the skills of the university's coaches and players to young soccer players aged seven to 18 in Edmonton communities. The academy runs summer soccer camps, international programs and a training program at the Vimy Ridge Academy School.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Investment_in_enhanced_facilities">Investment in enhanced facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Investment in enhanced facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Alberta is developing a new 2,403&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup> (25,870&nbsp;sq&nbsp;ft) fitness centre and state-of-the-art climbing complex as a part of the overall <b>Physical Activity and Wellness (PAW) Centre</b>, to be located at the corner of 87 Avenue and 114 Street on the university's North Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-PAW_Centre_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAW_Centre-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The PAW Centre will enhance student experience by providing a new indoor atrium and student lifestyle centre called the “social street,” created by enclosing the existing outdoor space between the main gymnasium, Universiade Pavilion and the East Wing of the Van Vliet Centre; additional student-focused multi-purpose space, including food retail, quiet study space, a games room, lounges, and a prayer and meditation space; and a variety of fitness components including individual and group training space, free weights, machine weights, stretching areas, cardio and fitness equipment, and locker-room renovations.<sup id="cite_ref-PAW_Centre_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAW_Centre-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distinguished_people">Distinguished people</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Distinguished people">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Alberta_people" title="List of University of Alberta people">List of University of Alberta people</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_University_of_Alberta" title="List of Presidents of the University of Alberta">List of Presidents of the University of Alberta</a>&nbsp;and 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chancellors_of_the_University_of_Alberta" title="List of Chancellors of the University of Alberta">List of Chancellors of the University of Alberta</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Faculty, staff and alumni of the University of Alberta have made significant contributions to society and have been recognized as international leaders in their fields.</p> 
     <p>Among the university's distinguished current and former faculty are authors <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Atwood" title="Margaret Atwood">Margaret Atwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/E._D._Blodgett" title="E. D. Blodgett">E. D. Blodgett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Botting" title="Gary Botting">Gary Botting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Hart" title="Jonathan Hart">Jonathan Hart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greg_Hollingshead" title="Greg Hollingshead">Greg Hollingshead</a>; bioethics pioneer <a href="/wiki/John_Dossetor" title="John Dossetor">John Dossetor</a>, physicists <a href="/wiki/Robert_William_Boyle" title="Robert William Boyle">Robert William Boyle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Werner_Israel" title="Werner Israel">Werner Israel</a>; biochemist <a href="/wiki/James_Collip" title="James Collip">James Collip</a> and chemist <a href="/wiki/Raymond_U._Lemieux" title="Raymond U. Lemieux" class="mw-redirect">Raymond Lemieux</a>; computer scientist <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Schaeffer" title="Jonathan Schaeffer">Jonathan Schaeffer</a> and paleontologist <a href="/wiki/Philip_J._Currie" title="Philip J. Currie">Philip Currie</a>.</p> 
     <p>Notable alumni include Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Richard_E._Taylor" title="Richard E. Taylor">Richard E. Taylor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Chief Justice of Canada <a href="/wiki/Beverley_McLachlin" title="Beverley McLachlin">Beverley McLachlin</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Daily_Planet_(TV_series)" title="Daily Planet (TV series)">Daily Planet</a> host <a href="/wiki/Jay_Ingram" title="Jay Ingram">Jay Ingram</a>, and Rhodes Scholar <a href="/wiki/George_Stanley" title="George Stanley">George Stanley</a>, who designed the Canadian flag.</p> 
     <p>Many University of Alberta alumni have gone on to prominence in politics, including former Canadian prime minister <a href="/wiki/Joe_Clark" title="Joe Clark">Joe Clark</a>, former governor general <a href="/wiki/Roland_Michener" title="Roland Michener">Roland Michener</a> and Alberta's 10th premier, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Lougheed" title="Peter Lougheed">Peter Lougheed</a>.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Alberta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <ul> 
      <li>William Hardy Alexander, <i>The University of Alberta: A Retrospect 1908–1929</i>. Edmonton: University Printing Press, 1929.</li> 
      <li>John MacDonald, <i>The History of the University of Alberta, 1908–1958</i>. Edmonton: University of Alberta, 1958, ASIN B0007EFODW.</li> 
      <li>Walter Johns, <i>History of the University of Alberta, 1908-1969</i>. Edmonton: University of Alberta Press, 1981, <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0888640250" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0-88864-025-0</a>.</li> 
      <li>Maureen Aytenfisu, &quot;The University of Alberta: Objectives, Structures, and Role, 1908–1928&quot; (MA thesis). University of Alberta, 1982.</li> 
      <li>Scott Rollans, <i>Echoes in the Halls: An Unofficial History of the University of Alberta</i>. Association of Professors Emeriti of the U of A, University Of Alberta, Nov. 1, 1999.</li> 
      <li>Ellen Schoeck, <i>I Was There: A Century of Alumni Stories About the University of Alberta, 1906–2006</i>. Edmonton: University of Alberta Press, 2006, <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0888644647" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0-88864-464-7</a>.</li> 
      <li>Rod MacLeod, <i>All True Things: A History of the University of Alberta, 1908–2008</i>. Edmonton: University of Alberta Press, 2008, <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780888644442" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-88864-444-2</a>.</li> 
     </ul>
